            <td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
              <div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
      </font></div>
            </td>
            <td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
              <div style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">2.</font></font></font></div>
            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">SUMMARY
      OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES</font></div>
            </td>
          </tr>
      </table>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Accounting
Principles.&#160;&#160;</font>The financial statements and accompanying notes
are prepared in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the
United States.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-ALIGN: justify" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Allowance For Doubtful
Accounts.&#160;&#160;</font>The allowance for doubtful accounts reflects PSI&#8217;s
best estimate of probable losses inherent in the accounts receivable
balance.&#160;&#160;PSI determines the allowance based on known troubled
accounts, historical experience, and other currently available
evidence.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Cash and Cash
Equivalents.&#160;&#160;</font>PSI considers all highly liquid interest-earning
investments with a maturity of three months or less at the date of purchase to
be cash equivalents.&#160;&#160;The fair value of these investments will
approximate their carrying value.&#160;&#160;In general, investments with
original maturities of greater than three months and remaining maturities of
less than one year will be classified as short-term
investments.&#160;&#160;Investments with maturities beyond one year may be
classified as short-term based on their highly liquid nature and because such
marketable securities represent the investment of cash that is available for
current operations.&#160;&#160;All cash equivalents and short-term investments
are classified as available for current operations.&#160;&#160;All cash
equivalents and short-term investments are classified as available for sale and
are recorded at market value using the specific identification
method.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Equity
and other investments may include both debt and equity
instruments.&#160;&#160;Debt securities and publicly traded equity securities
will be classified as available for sale and will be recorded at market using
the specific identification method.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Fair Value. </font>The carrying
amounts of cash and cash equivalents, trade receivables, accounts payable, notes
payable and accrued liabilities approximate fair value because of the short
maturity of these instruments.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Goodwill.&#160;&#160;</font>Goodwill
was tested for impairment during the fiscal year ended October 31, 2006 using a
fair-value-based approach.&#160;&#160;A full impairment of the goodwill was
identified and reflected in the statement of operations during the year
tested.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Income
Taxes.&#160;&#160;</font>Income taxes are calculated using the liability method
specified by Statement of Financial Accounting Standards (&#8220;SFAS&#8221;) No. 109,
&#8220;Accounting for Income Taxes.&#8221;&#160;&#160;The Company had deferred tax assets of
approximately $2,400,000 as of October 31, 2006, related primarily to net
operating loss carryforwards (&#8220;NOL&#8221;), which have yet to be
utilized.&#160;&#160;At October 31, 2006, the Company had an operating loss
carryforward of approximately $6,026,000, which expire through
2026.&#160;&#160;Also, the utilization of these losses, if available, to reduce
the future income taxes, will depend upon the generation of sufficient taxable
income prior to the expiration of the NOL.&#160;&#160;Therefore, at October 31,
2006, the Company established a 100% valuation allowance against the deferred
tax assets as the likelihood of recognizing this benefit cannot be
certain</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company has not filed federal or state income tax returns for the year ended
October 31, 2006.&#160;&#160;The Company does not expect to owe any taxes on
that return.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Inventories.&#160;&#160;</font>Inventories
are stated at the lower of cost or market, using the average cost
method.&#160;&#160;Cost includes materials, labor, and manufacturing overhead
related to the purchase and production of&#160;&#160;inventories.&#160;&#160;PSI
will regularly review inventory quantities on hand, future purchase commitments
with its suppliers, and the estimated utility of its inventory.&#160;&#160;If
such review indicates a reduction in utility below carrying value, PSI will
reduce its inventory to a new cost basis.&#160;&#160;The Company reflected a
reduction in the carrying value of the inventory as of October 31, 2006 totaling
$216,672, in order to reduce the carrying value to its net realization
value.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Loss per Common
Share.&#160;&#160;</font>In 1998, the Company adopted SFAS No. 128, &#8220;Earnings
Per Share&#8221; (&#8220;EPS&#8221;), which provides for the calculation of basic and diluted
EPS.&#160;&#160;Basic EPS includes no dilution and is computed by dividing the
income (loss) available to common stockholders by the weighted-average number of
common shares outstanding for the period.&#160;&#160;Diluted EPS reflects the
potential dilution of securities that could share in the income (loss) of the
Company.&#160;&#160;The effect of the potentially dilutive shares for the years
ended October 31, 2005 and 2006 have been ignored, as their effect would be
antidilutive.&#160;&#160;Potentially dilutive securities outstanding at October
31, 2005 and 2006 totaled 2,556,000 and 8,923,825, respectively.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Principles of
Consolidation.&#160;&#160;</font>The accompanying consolidated financial
statements include the accounts of PSI Corporation and its wholly owned
subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the &#8220;Company&#8221; or &#8220;PSI&#8221;) after
elimination of all significant intercompany balances and
transactions.&#160;&#160;Consolidated subsidiaries include friendlyway, Inc.
(December 2004, through May, 2006), and Big Fish Marketing Group, LLC (August,
2006, to the date hereof).</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Product
Warranty.&#160;&#160;</font>PSI provides for the estimated costs of hardware and
software warranties at the time the related revenue is
recognized.&#160;&#160;For hardware warranty, PSI estimates the costs based on
historical and projected project failure rates, historical and projected repair
costs, and knowledge of specific product failures (if any).&#160;&#160;The
specific hardware warranty terms and conditions vary depending upon the product
sold and country in which PSI will do business, but generally include technical
support, parts, and labor over a period generally ranging from 90 days to three
years.&#160;&#160;For software, PSI estimates the costs to provide bug fixes,
such as security patches, over the estimated life of the
software.&#160;&#160;PSI will regularly reevaluate its estimates to assess the
adequacy of the recorded warranty liabilities and adjust the amounts as
necessary. Sales subject to warranty were immaterial during the years ended
October 31, 2006.</font></div>
    <div><br></div>
    <div>
      <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">

          <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">18</font></div>
          <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
            <hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
          </div>
        </div>
        <div id="HDR">
          <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a href="#toc">Table of Contents</a></font></div>
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>
    <div><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Property and
Equipment.&#160;&#160;</font>Property and equipment is stated at cost and
depreciated using the straight-line method over the estimated life of
approximately five years.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Revenue
Recognition.&#160;&#160;</font>Revenue is recognized when persuasive evidence of
an arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the fee is fixed or determinable,
and collectibility is probable.&#160;&#160;In the event PSI should enter into
contracts where it is obligated to deliver multiple products and/or services,
total revenue will be generally allocated among the products based upon the sale
price of each product when sold separately.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In the
event PSI should in the future license or lease its products (rather than effect
outright sales of the same), revenue derived therefrom will be treated as
subscriptions, with billings recorded as unearned revenue and recognized as
revenue ratably over the billing coverage period.&#160;&#160;PSI&#8217;s potential
multiple year licensing/lease transactions may include the right to receive
future updated improvements to its product line.&#160;&#160;Some multi-year
licensing/lease arrangements may include a perpetual license for current
products combined with rights to receive future improved/updated versions of
such products.&#160;&#160;Online advertising revenue derived from the kiosks and
signage products are and will be recognized as advertisements are
displayed.&#160;&#160;Costs related to PSI&#8217;s product line are recognized when
the related revenue is recognized.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Use of Estimates and
Assumptions.&#160;&#160;</font>The preparation of financial statements in
conformity with generally accepted accounting principles requires management to
make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and
liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of
the financial statements, and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses
during the reporting period.&#160;&#160;Actual results could differ from those
estimates.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Concentration of Credit
Risk</font>.&#160;&#160;Financial instruments that potentially subject the
Company to concentrations of credit risk consist primarily of
cash.&#160;&#160;The Company maintains substantially all its cash balances in a
limited number of financial institutions.&#160;&#160;The balances are insured by
the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation up to $100,000.&#160;&#160;At October
31, 2006 and 2005, the Company&#8217;s did not have any uninsured balances, although
the balances may exceed the insured limits at times during the
year.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Recently
Issued Accounting Standards</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June,
2006, the FASB issued Interpretation No. 48 (&#8220;FIN No. 48&#8221;), <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Accounting for
Uncertainty</font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">in Income
Taxes &#8211; an interpretation of FASB Statement No. 109, </font>which clarifies the
accounting for uncertainty in income taxes recognized in an enterprise&#8217;s
financial statements in accordance with SFAS No. 109, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Accounting for Income
Taxes</font>.&#160;&#160;The Interpretation provides a recognition threshold and
measurement attribute for the financial statement recognition and measurement of
a tax position taken or expected to be taken in a tax return.&#160;&#160;Under
FIN No. 48, PSI may recognize the tax benefit from an uncertain tax position
only if it is more likely than not that the tax position will be sustained on
examination by the taxing authorities, based on the technical merits of the
position.&#160;&#160;The tax benefits recognized in the financial statements
from such a position should be measured based on the largest benefit that has a
greater than 50% likelihood of being realized upon ultimate
settlement.&#160;&#160;FIN No. 48 also provides guidance on derecognition,
classification, interest and penalties, accounting in interim periods,
disclosure and transition.&#160;&#160;FIN No. 48 is effective for PSI beginning
November 1, 2007.&#160;&#160;The adoption of FIN No. 48 is not expected to have
a material impact on the Company.&#160;&#160;.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June,
2006, the FASB ratified the Emerging Issues Task Force (&#8220;EITF&#8221;) consensus on
EITF issue No. 06-2, &#8220;Accounting for Sabbatical Leave and Other Similar Benefits
Pursuant to FASB Statement No. 43.&#8221;&#160;&#160;EITF Issue No. 06-2 requires
companies to accrue the costs of compensated absences under a sabbatical or
similar benefit arrangement over the requisite service period.&#160;&#160;EITF
Issue No. 06-2 is effective for PSI beginning November 1, 2007.&#160;&#160;The
cumulative effect of the application of this consensus on prior period results
should, in the future, be recognized through a cumulative-effect adjustment to
retained earnings as of the beginning of the year of
adoption.&#160;&#160;Elective retrospective application is also
permitted.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In fiscal
year 2007, we adopted Staff Accounting Bulletin (&#8220;SAB&#8221;) No. 108, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Considering the Effects of Prior
Year Misstatements when Quantifying Current Year
Misstatements.&#160;&#160;</font>SAB No. 108 requires companies to quantify
misstatements using both a balance sheet (iron curtain) and an income statement
(rollover) approach to evaluate whether either approach results in an error that
is material in light of relevant quantitative and qualitative factors, and
provides for a one-time cumulative effect transition adjustment.&#160;&#160;The
adoption of SAB No. 108 will not have an impact on PSI&#8217;s financial
statements.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
September, 2006, the FASB issued SFAS No. 157, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Fair Value Measurements,
</font>which defines fair value, establishes a framework for measuring fair
value in generally accepted accounting principles, and expands disclosures about
fair value measurements.&#160;&#160;SFAS No. 157 does not require any new fair
value measurements, but provides guidance on how to measure fair value by
providing a fair value hierarchy used to classify the source of the
information.&#160;&#160;This statement is effective for us beginning November 1,
2008.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">&#160;</div>
    <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
      <div id="FTR">
        <div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="center">

          <hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">

      <div id="HDR">
        <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a href="#toc">Table of Contents</a></font></div>
      </div>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
February, 2007 the FASB issued SFAS No. 159, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">The Fair Value Option for Financial
Assets and Financial Liabilities. </font>SFAS No. 159 will afford PSI the
irrevocable option to carry many financial assets and liabilities at fair
values, with changes in fair value recognized in earnings.&#160;&#160;No. 159
does not require any new fair value measurements, but provides guidance on how
to measure fair value by providing a fair value hierarchy used to classify the
source of the information.&#160;&#160;SFAS No. 159 is effective for PSI
beginning November 1, 2008, although earlier adoption is permitted.</font></div>
    <div>&#160;</div>

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">For the
fiscal years ended October 31, 2006 and 2005, depreciation expense,
respectively, amounted to $250 and $37,906.</font></div>

              <div style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">4.</font></font></font></div>
            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">INVENTORIES</font></div>

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 27pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Inventories
consist of the following:</font></div>

              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">STOCKHOLDERS&#8217;

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Stock Incentive
Plan.&#160;&#160;&#160;</font>The Company does not have a stock or option
incentive plan.&#160;&#160;Any grants of stock or options are made pursuant to
approval of the board of directors or shareholders, as applicable.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Increase
in Authorized Common Shares</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In April
2005, the Company filed an Amendment to its Articles of Incorporation to
increase the Company&#8217;s authorized shares to 100,000,000 shares of common stock,
par value $0.001 per share. There was no increase in the existing 5,000,000
authorized shares of preferred stock, par value $0.001 per share.&#160;&#160;In
September 2006, the Company filed an Amendment to its Articles of Incorporation
to increase the Company&#8217;s authorized shares to 300,000,000 shares of common
stock, par value $0.001 per share.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Common
Stock Issuances</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In April
2005, the Company entered into a Stock Purchase Agreement with a former officer
of the Company and sold 450,000 shares of the Company&#8217;s common stock for
$103,500.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
October 2006, the Company sold 5,000,000 shares of its common stock, pursuant to
an exemption from registration, at $.10 per share.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>

              <div style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">6.</font></font></font></div>
            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">ACQUISITIONS</font></div>
            </td>
          </tr>
      </table>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Since
inception, the corporate name of the Company has been changed
successively:&#160;&#160;Global Spill Management, Inc. (1991-1998); Biofarm,
Inc. (1998-2005); Friendlyway Corporation (2005-2006); and PSI Corporation
(2006-to date).&#160;&#160;Hereinafter, the Company is referred to as &#8220;PSI&#8221; or
the &#8220;Registrant.&#8221;&#160;&#160;The management of PSI as of the date hereof assumed
their respective offices subsequent to the transactions described in this
note.</font></div>
    <div><br></div>
    <div>
      <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
        <div id="FTR">
          <div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="center">

        <div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
          <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">20</font></div>
          <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
            <hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
          </div>
        </div>
        <div id="HDR">
          <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a href="#toc">Table of Contents</a></font></div>
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>
    <div><br></div>
    <div>
      <table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%">
          <tr valign="top">
            <td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
              <div style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">A)</font></div>
            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Failed Acquisition of
      Pantel</font>.&#160;&#160;As previously reported in Form 8-K and Form
      8-K/A filings dated respectively, May 3, 2006, and July 12, 2006,
      Friendlyway Corporation (&#8220;FC&#8221;) entered into an agreement, dated April 27,
      2006, to acquire 100% of the capital stock of Pantel Systems, Inc.
      (&#8220;Pantel&#8221;).&#160;&#160;Such agreement was manifestly deficient in that it
      contained inadequate representations and warranties, it did not require
      the receipt by FC of audited financial statements of Pantel for the
      preceding two-year period, its escrow provisions (the deposit into an
      escrow account of an aggregate of 8,600,000 of the twenty million shares
      to be issued by FC in exchange for 100% of Pantel) were not complied with,
      and its very execution was violative of Rule 14f-1 (1934 Act) and Item
      9.01 of Form 8-K.</font></div>
            </td>
          </tr>
      </table>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 18pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">For
accounting purposes, Pantel would have been considered the acquiring party had
the agreement to acquire Pantel been effective.&#160;&#160;In such event, the
Pantel acquisition would have been accounted for as a reverse purchase in
accordance with Generally Acted Accounting Principles (GAPP) and with the
management of Pantel in control of PSI.&#160;&#160;Notwithstanding the
deficiencies in the agreement noted above, the management of Pantel became the
directors and officers of PSI. Simultaneously with the acquisition of Pantel,
PSI ceased all of its operating activities and friendlyway, Inc. (its sole
operating subsidiary) discontinued its operations.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 18pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Predicated
upon a legal opinion received by the present management of PSI concerning the
legal status of the 20,000,000 shares of PSI Common Stock to be issued by PSI in
exchange for 100% of the Pantel capital stock, the present management of PSI
considers the failed acquisition of Pantel to have been a nullity, to have been
void <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">ab initio</font>, and to
have never been consummated.&#160;&#160;Accordingly, the accounts and operations
of Pantel (which, in any event were <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">de minimis)</font> have been omitted
from PSI&#8217;s consolidated financial statements.&#160;&#160;All Common Stock and
per share amounts from the date of the failed acquisition of Pantel to October
31, 2006, have been retroactively adjusted to reflect the nullification of the
issuance of the 20,000,000 PSI shares.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 18pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">With
respect to the accounting issue presented by the rescission, effective October
31, 2006, of the proposed Pantel transaction, namely, whether rescission voids
the proposed Pantel transaction <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">nunc pro tunc</font> or whether
recession requires treatment of the Pantel acquisition as a discontinued
operation requiring inclusion of Pantel in the PSI consolidated financial
statements for the fiscal year ended October 31, 2006, PSI believes that such
decision must be decided upon the facts peculiar to the proposed Pantel
transaction.&#160;&#160;In that regard, PSI learned that the Escrow Agreement
included as part of the Pantel acquisition agreement, was never actually
consummated.&#160;&#160;The designated escrow agent received neither the
8,600,000 PSI shares nor 100% of the capital stock of Pantel.&#160;&#160;The
failure to deliver a certificate representing 100% of the capital stock of
Pantel is evidence that PSI never took possession of Pantel and cannot be deemed
ever to have controlled Pantel.&#160;&#160;The foregoing failures support the
PSI position that the proposed Pantel acquisition was void <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">ab initio</font>.&#160;&#160;The
legal opinion received by PSI supports this conclusion.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 18pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Additional
evidence of the failure to consummate the proposed acquisition of Pantel
consists of the following:</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div>
      <table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%">
          <tr valign="top">
            <td style="WIDTH: 36pt">
              <div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
      </font></div>
            </td>
            <td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
              <div style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">i.</font></div>
            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">the
      July 12, 2006, Form 8-K/A filing of PSI signed by the sole shareholder of
      Pantel specifically states that &#8220;no shares of common stock have been
      issued to consummate the acquisition of Pantel&#8221; and that the obligation to
      deliver to the escrow agent has not been honored.&#160;&#160;No subsequent
      Form 8-K filing reflects either the issuance of the 20,000,000 PSI shares
      or the failure to deliver to the escrow
agent;</font></div>
            </td>
          </tr>
      </table>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div>
      <table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%">
          <tr valign="top">
            <td style="WIDTH: 36pt">
              <div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
      </font></div>
            </td>
            <td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
              <div style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">ii.</font></div>
            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">all
      of the 20,000,000 PSI shares delivered to the sole shareholder of Pantel
      have been returned to PSI and the directors and officers of PSI named by
      Pantel have resigned;</font></div>
            </td>
          </tr>
      </table>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div>
      <table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%">
          <tr valign="top">
            <td style="WIDTH: 36pt">
              <div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
      </font></div>
            </td>
            <td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
              <div style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">iii.</font></div>
            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Rule
      14f-1 of the 1934 Act was violated when the Pantel management, then in
      control of PSI, failed to advise the SEC of the change in the majority of
      the Board of Directors of PSI and that such change was not approved by the
      Shareholders of PSI;</font></div>
            </td>
          </tr>
      </table>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div>
      <table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%">
          <tr valign="top">
            <td style="WIDTH: 36pt">
              <div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
      </font></div>
            </td>
            <td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
              <div style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">iv.</font></div>
            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Neither
      the Form 8-K nor the Form 9-K/A filings signed by the solo shareholder of
      Pantel contained the audited financial statements of Pantel required to be
      filed by Item 9.01 of Form 8-K;
and,</font></div>
            </td>
          </tr>
      </table>
    </div>

    <div>
      <table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%">
          <tr valign="top">
            <td style="WIDTH: 36pt">
              <div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
      </font></div>
            </td>
            <td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
              <div style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">v.</font></div>
            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
      sole shareholder of Pantel did not comply with the requirement to file
      Schedule 13D pursuant to the 1934 Act, indicating his ownership of more
      than five (5%) of the issued and outstanding shares of PSI Common
      Stock.</font></div>
            </td>
          </tr>
      </table>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 18pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Predicated
upon all of the foregoing, PSI has concluded that the proposed transaction
between PSI and Pantel never, in point of fact, was consummated pursuant to the
May 3, 2006, agreement.&#160;&#160;Therefore, the operations of Pantel never
belonged to PSI and should not be included in the PSI financial statements for
the fiscal period ended October 31, 2006, and the fiscal year ended October 31,
2007.</font></div>

              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Failed Acquisition of
      Ignition Media Group, LLC</font>.&#160;&#160;As previously reported in a
      Form 8-K filing dated August 25, 2006, a wholly-owned subsidiary of FC
      entered into an Asset Purchase Agreement (&#8220;ASP&#8221;), dated August 22, 2006,
      to acquire substantially all of the assets of Ignition Media Group, LLC
      (&#8220;IMG&#8221;), a Pennsylvania limited liability company.&#160;&#160;The
      Registrant was not a signatory to such ASP.&#160;&#160;The wholly-owned
      subsidiary of the Registrant agreed to purchase the assets of IMG for
      $1,000,000 in cash and an aggregate of 6,818,182 shares of the parent
      Registrant&#8217;s Common Stock.&#160;&#160;The $1,000,000 was to have been paid
      in twelve equal monthly installments of $83,333.33 each.&#160;&#160;The
      initial installment payment was made at closing.&#160;&#160;The 6,818,182
      shares of the Registrant&#8217;s Common Stock were represented as having an
      agreed aggregate value of $1,500,000.&#160;&#160;Thus, the aggregate
      consideration to be paid by the subsidiary for the assets of IMG amounted
      to $2,500,000 plus the assumption of $180,000 in
  debt.</font></div>

Act filings and that, therefore, Rule 144 was not applicable to the remaining
3,318,182 shares.&#160;&#160;The SAR also obligated the Registrant to pay to IMG
the additional sum of $100,000.&#160;&#160;(In some instances, references herein

reported in a Form 8-K filing dated November 22, 2006, the Registrant and CA

lawsuit initiated on October 18, 2006, by CA against the
subsidiary.&#160;&#160;The Registrant was not named as a party defendant in the
action instituted by CA.&#160;&#160;The subsidiary of the Registrant, an entity
known as Pantel Systems, Inc., and Friendlyway Inc., a former subsidiary, the
operations of which ceased as of July 31, 2006, were the named
defendants.&#160;&#160;The lawsuit alleged that the purchase of the assets of CA
by the subsidiary pursuant to the ASP originally dated May 18, 2006, the
addendum thereto dated August 10, 2006, and the closing thereof dated August 22,
2006, resulted in the default by the subsidiary in the payment of $872,809.95 of
the cash portion of the purchase price for CA.&#160;&#160;The lawsuit also
alleged the failure by the subsidiary to deliver to CA the 5,909,591 shares of
the Registrant&#8217;s Common Stock.</font></div>

provided for the rescission of the transaction between CA and the subsidiary,
the retention by CA of $195,000 of the cash portion of the purchase price
previously received by CA, and the payment of the additional sum of $90,000 to
CA.&#160;&#160;CA agreed to relinquish all right, title and interest in and to
the 5,909,591 shares of Common Stock to be issued to CA and to surrender the
promissory note it had previously received at closing in the amount of
$872,809.85.&#160;&#160;(In some instances, reference herein to CA refers to the
shareholder(s) thereof.)</font></div>

          <tr valign="top">
            <td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
              <div style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">B)</font></div>
            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">On
      April 27, 2007, FWAG, a German corporation that had received 6,000,000 of
      the aggregate of 18,000,000 shares issued by the Company effective
      December 10, 2004, in exchange for 100% of the capital stock of
      friendlyway, Inc. (&#8220;FWI&#8221;), sued the Company in California Superior Court
      in response to the Company&#8217;s attempted cancellation of the shares received
      by FWAG.&#160;&#160;The Company then instituted a separate action in
      California Federal District Court (No. C 07 02869 SBA) on June 1, 2007,
      against FWAG in which the Company alleged that it was fraudulently induced
      to acquire FWI and to issue 18,000,000 shares of its Common Stock in
      exchange therefore.&#160;&#160;The Company sought rescission of the FWI
      transaction and, to prevent irreparable harm, moved on June 5, 2007, for a
      temporary restraining order to attempt to preserve the status
      quo.&#160;&#160;(The named defendants in the Federal action were believed
      to own an aggregate of 15,576,000 of the 18,000,000
    shares.)</font></div>
            </td>
          </tr>
      </table>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 18pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The law
is settled that a party seeking a temporary restraining order must demonstrate
either (a) the combination of probable success on the merits or (b) serious
issues being raised and the balance of hardships being in favor of the
movant.&#160;&#160;The Court ruled that the Company failed to show a likelihood
of success on the Merits, that the securities fraud and breach of contract
claims were time-barred, and that its allegations of fraud were precatory and,
therefore, unsupported.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 18pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Subsequently,
the Company was constrained to execute settlement agreements with each of the
four named defendants.&#160;&#160;Such settlements resolved the litigation
instituted both by AG and by the Company.&#160;&#160;Each such settlement
agreement differed in content and result and in the disposition of the shares of
Common Stock in issue.&#160;&#160;In sum, the settlements resulted in the net
cancellation of 4,401,906 shares of Common Stock and the release of AG claims to
an additional 18 million shares thereof.&#160;&#160;The Company believes it to
be significant that its then counsel did not raise the issues of (a) failure to
deliver consideration by the shareholders of FWI and (b) damages sustained by
the Company as the proximate cause of all AG-appointed Company directors
resigning in December, 2006, resulting in only one director of the Company
remaining and that such one director initiated the transaction that resulted in
the dissipation of Company assets, the decline in the Company&#8217;s stock price, and
the necessity that present management (from January, 2007) be compelled to
effect a reorganization of the Company.</font></div>

            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Additional
      litigation matters are discussed in Note 6 (Acquisitions).&#160;&#160;The

              <div style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">8.</font></font></font></div>
            </td>
            <td>
              <div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">DEBT</font></div>
            </td>

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Round
A Secured Term Loans</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In August
2006, the Company entered into secured term notes (&#8220;Round A Notes&#8221;) with several
unrelated parties totaling $282,500.&#160;&#160;The Round A Notes were due on
February 18, 2009 and incurred an interest rate of the greater of 12% per annum
or the prime interest rate plus 4%.&#160;&#160;Among other provisions, the Round
A Notes provided for monthly repayments of principle and interest over a 28
month period commencing in October 2006.&#160;&#160;The Company failed to make
the required payments at that time.&#160;&#160;Pursuant to the default
provisions of the note, the Company incurred a 25% default penalty payment of
the then outstanding balance.&#160;&#160;The Company recorded a $43,750 penalty
during the year ended October 31, 2006 which it reflected as additional interest
expense.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
connection with the Round A Notes, the Company also issued warrants to purchase
4,900,000 shares of the Company&#8217;s common stock at an exercise price of
$.01.&#160;&#160;The warrants may be exercisable at any time for a period of 7
years.&#160;&#160;In connection with the issuance of the warrants, the Company
has reflected a value for the warrants of $96,023.&#160;&#160;The fair value of
the warrant grant was estimated on the date of the grant using the Black-Scholes
option-pricing model with the following weighted average assumptions: expected
volatility of 15%, risk free interest rate of 4.86%; and expected lives of 5
years. The warrants meet the requirements to be classified as
equity.&#160;&#160;The value of the warrants was reflected as additional
interest and expensed on the date of issuance.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In August
2007, the Company entered into exchange agreements with the holders of the Round
A Notes whereby the notes were converted into 2,280,500 shares of the Company&#8217;s
common stock.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Round
B-1 Convertible Term Loans</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In July
2006, the Company entered into convertible term notes (&#8220;Round B-1 Notes&#8221;) with
several unrelated parties totaling $830,000.&#160;&#160;The Round B-1 Notes were
due on January 19, 2009 and incurred an interest rate of 14% per
annum.&#160;&#160;Among other provisions, the Round B-1 Notes provided for
monthly repayments of principle and interest over a 28 month period commencing
in October 2006.&#160;&#160;The Company failed to make the required payments at
that time.&#160;&#160;Pursuant to the default provisions of the note, the
Company incurred a 25% default penalty payment of the then outstanding
balance.&#160;&#160;The Company recorded a $207,500 penalty during the year
ended October 31, 2006 which it reflected as additional interest
expense.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
connection with the Round B-1 Notes, the Company also issued warrants to
purchase 1,976,191 shares of the Company&#8217;s common stock at an exercise price of
$.19.&#160;&#160;The warrants may be exercisable at any time for a period of 5
years.&#160;&#160;In connection with the issuance of the warrants, the Company
has reflected a value for the warrants of $41,912.&#160;&#160;The fair value of
the warrant grant was estimated on the date of the grant using the Black-Scholes
option-pricing model with the following weighted average assumptions: expected
volatility of 15%, risk free interest rate of 5.06%; and expected lives of 2.5
years. The warrants meet the requirements to be classified as
equity.&#160;&#160;The value of the warrants was reflected as additional
interest and expensed on the date of issuance.</font></div>
    <div><br></div>
    <div>
      <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
        <div id="FTR">

          <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
            <hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
          </div>
        </div>
        <div id="HDR">
          <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a href="#toc">Table of Contents</a></font></div>
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>
    <div><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In August
2007, the Company entered into exchange agreements with the holders of the Round
B-1 Notes whereby the notes were converted into 8,300,000 shares of the
Company&#8217;s common stock.&#160;&#160;In addition, the warrants were exchanged for
new warrants to purchase 1,976,191 shares of the Company&#8217;s common stock which
may be exercised at any time over a 5 year period at an exercise price of $.19
per share.&#160;&#160;No additional expense was recorded for these warrants as
the additional cost was not material.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">&#160;</div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Round
B-2 Convertible Term Loans</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
October 2006, the Company entered into convertible term notes (&#8220;Round B-2
Notes&#8221;) with several unrelated parties totaling approximately
$960,000.&#160;&#160;The Round B-2 Notes were due on November 11, 2009 and
incurred an interest rate of 14% per annum.&#160;&#160;Among other provisions,
the Round B-2 Notes provided for monthly repayments of principle and interest
over a 28 month period commencing in December 2006.&#160;&#160;The Company
failed to make the required payments at that time.&#160;&#160;Pursuant to the
default provisions of the note, the Company incurred a 25% default penalty
payment of the then outstanding balance.&#160;&#160;The Company recorded a
$240,000 penalty during the year ended October 31, 2007 which it reflected as
additional interest expense.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
connection with the Round B-2 Notes, the Company also issued warrants to
purchase 2,047,634 shares of the Company&#8217;s common stock at an exercise price of
$.14.&#160;&#160;The warrants may be exercisable at any time for a period of 5
years.&#160;&#160;In connection with the issuance of the warrants, the Company
has not reflected a value for the warrants as the value was not
material.&#160;&#160;The fair value of the warrant grant was estimated on the
date of the grant using the Black-Scholes option-pricing model with the
following weighted average assumptions: expected volatility of 15%, risk free
interest rate of 5.06%; and expected lives of 2.5 years.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In August
2007, the Company entered into exchange agreements with the holders of the Round
B-1 Notes whereby the notes were converted into 9,599,980 shares of the
Company&#8217;s common stock.&#160;&#160;In addition, the warrants were exchanged for
new warrants to purchase 2,047,634 shares of the Company&#8217;s common stock which
may be exercised at any time over a 5 year period at an exercise price of $.19
per share.&#160;&#160;No additional expense was recorded for these warrants as
the additional cost was not material.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Big
Fish Notes</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In May
and June 2006, the Company entered into notes payable aggregating $45,000 with
two unrelated parties.&#160;&#160;The notes are due three years from the date of
issuance and incur interest at the rate of 10% per annum.&#160;&#160;Interest on
the notes is payable on a quarterly basis.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Shelter
Island Opportunity Fund Notes</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In August
2006, the Company entered into a note agreement for the payment of consulting
fees to an unrelated party totaling $98,770.&#160;&#160;The note is due on
October 31, 2008 with 11 monthly payments commencing on January 31, 2007 and
incurs interest at the rate of 12.25% per annum.&#160;&#160;Interest on the
notes is payable on a monthly basis commencing November 30, 2007.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Miller
Financial Network Note</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June
2006, the Company entered into a note agreement with an unrelated party totaling
$100,000.&#160;&#160;The note incurred interest at the rate of 10% per
annum.&#160;&#160;In January 2007, the Company was notified that the note was in
default and the holder had elected to accelerate the note.&#160;&#160;The
Company has been making payments monthly payments towards the interest, legal
costs and principle on the note.&#160;&#160;At October 31, 2007, there was
$97,800 in principle remaining on the note.</font></div>

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-ALIGN: justify" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Settlement with Former Chief
Financial Officer</font>.&#160;&#160;On June 13, 2008, Henry C. Lo, the former
Chief Financial Officer of Friendlyway Corporation, completed his obligations
pursuant to a settlement agreement executed in November, 2007, that terminated
litigation instituted by the Registrant against him.&#160;&#160;Mr. Lo delivered
to the Registrant 700,000 shares of Registrant&#8217;s Common Stock and $20,000 in
cash.&#160;&#160;The settlement agreement did not purport to extinguish any
claims by the Registrant arising out of the FWI transaction and the resolution
thereof.&#160;&#160;See Note 6 (&#8220;Acquisitions&#8221;).</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Bridge
Loans</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
February and March 2007, the Company entered into notes (&#8220;Bridge Notes&#8221;) with
several unrelated parties totaling approximately $325,000.&#160;&#160;The Bridge
Notes were due on November 11, 2009 and incurred an interest rate of 12% per
annum.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In August
2007, the Company entered into exchange agreements with the holders of 300,000
of the Bridge Notes whereby the notes were converted into 3,000,000 shares of
the Company&#8217;s common stock.&#160;&#160;The remaining $25,000 remains outstanding
at October 31, 2007.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Round
D Loans</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">From May
through October 2007, the Company entered into notes (&#8220;Round D Notes&#8221;) with
several unrelated parties totaling approximately $1,520,000.&#160;&#160;The
Round D Notes were incur interest at a rate of 12% per annum, payable
semi-annually.&#160;&#160;Subsequent to October 31, 2007, the Company sold an
additional $1,075,000 of the Round D Notes.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left">
      <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="9">ITEM </a>9.&#160; </font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">CHANGES
IN AND DISAGREEMENTS WITH ACCOUNTANTS ON ACCOUNTING AND FINANCIAL
DISCLOSURE</font></div>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">None.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left">
      <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold"><a name="9at">ITEM </a>9A(T).&#160;
</font></font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">CONTROLS AND
PROCEDURES</font></font></div>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Evaluation of Disclosure Controls
and Procedures</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Under the
supervision and with the participation of our management, including our
principal executive officer and principal accounting officer, we conducted an
evaluation of the effectiveness of the design and operation of our disclosure
controls and procedures, as defined in Rules 13a-15(e) and 15d-15(e) under the
Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as of October 31, 2006 (the &#8220;Evaluation Date&#8221;).
Based on this evaluation, our principal executive officer and principal
accounting officer concluded as of the Evaluation Date that our disclosure
controls and procedures were effective such that the material information
required to be included in our Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) reports
is recorded, processed, summarized and reported within the time periods
specified in SEC rules and forms relating to us, including our consolidated
subsidiary, and was made known to them by others within those entities,
particularly during the period when this report was being prepared.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">There
were no changes in our internal controls or in other factors that could
significantly affect these controls subsequent to the Evaluation
Date.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Management&#8217;s Report on Internal
Control over Financial Reporting</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">We are
responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over
financial reporting (as defined in Rule 13a-15(f) or 15d-15(f) under the
Exchange Act). Under the supervision and with the participation of our
management, including our principal executive officer and chief financial
officer, we conducted an evaluation of the effectiveness of our internal control
over financial reporting based on the framework in <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Internal Controls &#8212; Integrated
Framework </font>issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the
Treadway Commission, and the related guidance provided in <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Internal Control Over Financial
Reporting &#8212; Guidance for Smaller Public Companies </font>also issued by the
Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission.</font></div>
    <div><br></div>
    <div>
      <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
        <div id="FTR">
          <div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="center">

        </div>
        <div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
          <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">25</font></div>
          <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
            <hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
          </div>
        </div>
        <div id="HDR">
          <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-STYLE: italic; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a href="#toc">Table of Contents</a></font></div>
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>
    <div><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Our
internal control over financial reporting is a process designed to provide
reasonable assurance regarding the preparation and fair presentation of
financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted
accounting principles. Internal control over financial reporting includes those
policies and procedures that (i) pertain to the maintenance of records that in
reasonable detail accurately and fairly reflect the transactions and
dispositions of our assets; (ii) provide reasonable assurance that transactions
are recorded as necessary to permit preparation of financial statements in
accordance with generally accepted accounting principles, and that our receipts
and expenditures are being made only in accordance with authorizations of our
management and directors; and (iii) provide reasonable assurance regarding
prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use or disposition
of our assets that could have a material effect on the financial
statements.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Because
of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not
prevent or detect misstatements. Also, projections of any evaluation of
effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become
inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that the degree of compliance
with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Based on
our evaluation under the framework in <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Internal Controls &#8212; Integrated
Framework</font>, our management concluded that our internal control over
financial reporting was effective as of October 31, 2006.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">This
annual report does not include an attestation report of our independent
registered public accounting firm regarding internal control over financial
reporting. Our internal control over financial reporting was not subject to
attestation by our independent registered public accounting firm pursuant to
temporary rules of the SEC that permit us to provide only management&#8217;s report in
this annual report.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="9b">ITEM </a>9B.&#160;&#160;OTHER INFORMATION</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">None.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">PART III</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left">
      <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="10"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">ITEM</font>&#160;</a><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">10.&#160;</font>&#160;</font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">DIRECTORS, EXECUTIVE OFFICERS AND
CORPORATE GOVERNANCE</font></font></div>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
executive officers, directors and key personnel of the Company as of October 31,
2006, are as follows:</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-STYLE: italic">David Lott,
Chairman of the Board</font>.&#160;&#160;Mr. Lott was appointed as our Chairman
of the Board in July 2006.&#160;&#160;Mr. Lott, with 20 years experience in
business development and management in both the private and public sector, has
been a mainstay in the digital signage industry since founding Limelight Media
Group, Inc. in 1999. He held the position of Chairman and Chief Executive
Officer of the public company until June 2005, when he orchestrated Limelight&#8217;s
acquisition of Impart, Inc., creating Impart Media Group. Lott remained as CEO
of Impart during the integration of the combined companies until his departure
in March 2006.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-STYLE: italic">Kenneth Upcraft,
President, Chief Executive Officer and Director. </font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">&#160;</font>Mr. Upcraft was
appointed as our President, Chief Executive Officer and Director in May
2006.&#160;&#160;Since its inception in February 2005, Mr. Upcraft served as
president and chief executive of Pantel Systems, Inc. Mr. Upcraft served as
president of USURF America, Inc. from April 2002 until August 2004. Mr. Upcraft
served as vice president of Netbeam from February 2001 until March 2002. From
June 1993 until March 2001, Mr. Upcraft operated a consultancy focused on
providing professional services to telecommunications and Internet service
providers, including wireless Internet access providers.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">No
director, officer or affiliate of the Company is an adverse party to the Company
or any of its subsidiaries in any material proceeding.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company&#8217;s Board of Directors does not have an audit committee and no
determination has been made as to whether any member of the Board of Directors
qualifies as an audit committee financial expert as defined in Item 401 of
Regulation S-B.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Section
16(a) Beneficial Ownership Reporting Compliance</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Section
16(a) of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended, requires that our
directors and executive officers and persons who beneficially own more than 10%
of our common stock (referred to herein as the &#8220;reporting persons&#8221;) file with
the SEC various reports as to their ownership of and activities relating to our
common stock. Such reporting persons are required by the SEC regulations to
furnish us with copies of all Section 16(a) reports they file. Based solely upon
a review of copies of Section 16(a) reports and representations received by us
from reporting persons, and without conducting any independent investigation of
our own, in 2006 and 2005, we believe all Forms 3, 4 and 5 were timely filed
with the SEC by such reporting persons.</font></div>

of Ethics</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
